# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Envoy xDS Aggregated Discovery Service Server

## Your Task

Find all C++ source files in envoyproxy/envoy that implement the ADS (Aggregated Discovery Service) gRPC server: the gRPC stream handler, the resource subscription tracking, the delta-xDS state machine, and the ACK/NACK processing.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the platform domain.

The answer file `/workspace/answer.json` contains:

### **32 C++ Source Files** organized by component:

1. **gRPC Stream Handler** (2 files): `grpc_stream.h`, `grpc_stream_interface.h`
   - Manages bidirectional gRPC communication with rate limiting and reconnection

2. **Main Mux Implementations** (6 files): Legacy (SotW and Delta) and unified template-based implementations
   - `grpc_mux_impl.h/cc`: Legacy SotW mux
   - `new_grpc_mux_impl.h/cc`: New Delta mux
   - `xds_mux/grpc_mux_impl.h/cc`: Unified template mux

3. **Subscription State Machine** (7 files): Implements both SotW and Delta xDS protocols
   - Base interface: `subscription_state.h`
   - SotW: `sotw_subscription_state.h/cc`
   - Delta: `delta_subscription_state.h/cc` (both unified and legacy versions)

4. **Resource Watch Tracking** (2 files): `watch_map.h/cc`
   - Manages multiple resource watchers and subscription interest changes

5. **ACK/NACK Processing** (3 files):
   - `update_ack.h`: ACK/NACK data structure
   - `pausable_ack_queue.h/cc`: Head-of-line blocking mitigation with pause support

6. **Supporting Components** (12+ files): Failover, factories, context, caching, etc.

Each of those subscriptions is viewed as a \"watch\" on X, while behind the scenes\n49: // there is just a single real subscription to that resource name.\n50: //\n51: // This class maintains the watches<-->subscription mapping: it\n52: // 1) delivers updates to all interested watches, and\n53: // 2) tracks which resource names should be {added to,removed from} the subscription when the\n54: //    {first,last} watch on a resource name is {added,removed}.\n55: //\n56: // #1 is accomplished by WatchMap's implementation of the SubscriptionCallbacks interface.\n57: // This interface allows the xDS client to just throw each xDS update message it receives directly\n58: // into WatchMap::onConfigUpdate, rather than having to track the various watches' callbacks.\n59: //\n60: // The information for #2 is returned by updateWatchInterest(); the caller should use it to\n61: // update the subscription accordingly.\n62: //\n63: // A WatchMap is assumed to be dedicated to a single type_url type of resource (EDS, CDS, etc).\n64: //\n65: // The WatchMap can also store the fetched resources in a cache, and allow others to fetch\n66: // resources directly from the cache. This is done for EDS in the following case:\n67: // Assume an active EDS cluster exists with some load-assignment that is kept in the cache.\n68: // If the cluster is updated, and no load-assignment is sent from the xDS server, the\n69: // cached version will be used.\n70: // The WatchMap is responsible to update the cache with the resource contents, and it is\n71: // up to the specific xDS type subscription handler (i.e., EdsClusterImpl), to fetch\n72: // the resource from the cache.\n73: class WatchMap : public UntypedConfigUpdateCallbacks, public Logger::Loggable<Logger::Id::config> {\n74: public:\n75:   WatchMap(const bool use_namespace_matching, const std::string& type_url,\n76:            CustomConfigValidators& config_validators, EdsResourcesCacheOptRef eds_resources_cache)\n77:       : use_namespace_matching_(use_namespace_matching), type_url_(type_url),\n78:         config_validators_(config_validators), eds_resources_cache_(eds_resources_cache) {\n79:     // If eds resources cache is provided, then the type must be ClusterLoadAssignment.\n80:     ASSERT(!eds_resources_cache_.has_value() ||\n81:            (type_url == Config::getTypeUrl<envoy::config::endpoint::v3::ClusterLoadAssignment>()));\n82:   }\n83: \n84:   // Adds 'callbacks' to the WatchMap, with every possible resource being watched.\n85:   // (Use updateWatchInterest() to narrow it down to some specific names).\n86:   // Returns the newly added watch, to be used with updateWatchInterest and removeWatch.\n87:   Watch* addWatch(SubscriptionCallbacks& callbacks, OpaqueResourceDecoder& resource_decoder);\n88: \n89:   // Updates the set of resource names that the given watch should watch.\n90:   // Returns any resource name additions/removals that are unique across all watches. That is:\n91:   // 1) if 'resources' contains X and no other watch cares about X, X will be in added_.\n92:   // 2) if 'resources' does not contain Y, and this watch was the only one that cared about Y,\n93:   //    Y will be in removed_.\n94:   AddedRemoved updateWatchInterest(Watch* watch,\n95:                                    const absl::flat_hash_set<std::string>& update_to_these_names);\n96: \n97:   // Expects that the watch to be removed has already had all of its resource names removed via\n98:   // updateWatchInterest().\n99:   void removeWatch(Watch* watch);\n100: \n101:   // UntypedConfigUpdateCallbacks.\n102:   void onConfigUpdate(const Protobuf::RepeatedPtrField<ProtobufWkt::Any>& resources,\n103:                       const std::string& version_info) override;\n104: \n105:   void onConfigUpdate(const std::vector<DecodedResourcePtr>& resources,\n106:                       const std::string& version_info) override;\n107: \n108:   void onConfigUpdate(\n109:       const Protobuf::RepeatedPtrField<envoy::service::discovery::v3::Resource>& added_resources,\n110:       const Protobuf::RepeatedPtrField<std::string>& removed_resources,\n111:       const std::string& system_version_info) override;\n112:   void onConfigUpdateFailed(ConfigUpdateFailureReason reason, const EnvoyException* e) override;\n113: \n114:   WatchMap(const WatchMap&) = delete;\n115:   WatchMap& operator=(const WatchMap&) = delete;\n116: \n117: private:\n118:   void removeDeferredWatches();\n119: \n120:   // Given a list of names that are new to an individual watch, returns those names that are in fact\n121:   // new to the entire subscription.\n122:   absl::flat_hash_set<std::string>\n123:   findAdditions(const absl::flat_hash_set<std::string>& newly_added_to_watch, Watch* watch);\n124: \n125:   // Given a list of names that an individual watch no longer cares about, returns those names that\n126:   // in fact the entire subscription no longer cares about.\n127:   absl::flat_hash_set<std::string>\n128:   findRemovals(const absl::flat_hash_set<std::string>& newly_removed_from_watch, Watch* watch);\n129: \n130:   // Returns the union of watch_interest_[resource_name] and wildcard_watches_.\n131:   absl::flat_hash_set<Watch*> watchesInterestedIn(const std::string& resource_name);\n132: \n133:   absl::flat_hash_set<std::unique_ptr<Watch>> watches_;\n134: \n135:   // Watches whose interest set is currently empty, which is interpreted as \"everything\".\n136:   absl::flat_hash_set<Watch*> wildcard_watches_;\n137: \n138:   // Watches that have been removed inside the call stack of the WatchMap's onConfigUpdate(). This\n139:   // can happen when a watch's onConfigUpdate() results in another watch being removed via\n140:   // removeWatch().\n141:   std::unique_ptr<absl::flat_hash_set<Watch*>> deferred_removed_during_update_;\n142: \n143:   // Maps a resource name to the set of watches interested in that resource. `grpc_stream_interface.h`\\n\\nThe `GrpcStream<RequestProto, ResponseProto>` template class manages the gRPC bidirectional streaming communication with the xDS management server. It handles stream establishment, message sending, rate limiting, reconnection with backoff, and status tracking. The `GrpcStreamInterface` provides the abstract interface for stream operations.\\n\\n## 2. Main gRPC Mux Implementations\\n\\n### Legacy Implementation (Two variants):\\n**Files**: `source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/grpc_mux_impl.h/cc`, `new_grpc_mux_impl.h/cc`\\n\\n- `GrpcMuxImpl` handles State-of-the-World (SotW) xDS protocol where the entire resource state is sent with each update\\n- `NewGrpcMuxImpl` handles Delta xDS protocol where only resource changes are sent\\n\\nThese manage subscription multiplexing, request queuing, and ACK/NACK handling.\\n\\n### Unified Implementation (New Architecture):\\n**Files**: `source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/xds_mux/grpc_mux_impl.h/cc`\\n\\nThe template-based `GrpcMuxImpl<S, F, RQ, RS>` provides a unified mux that handles both SotW and Delta variants through template parameters:\\n- `GrpcMuxSotw`: Specialization for SotW protocol\\n- `GrpcMuxDelta`: Specialization for Delta protocol\\n\\n## 3. Subscription State Machine (Resource Subscription Tracking)\\n**Files**: `source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/xds_mux/subscription_state.h`, `sotw_subscription_state.h/cc`, `delta_subscription_state.h/cc`\\n\\n- `BaseSubscriptionState<RS, RQ>`: Abstract base for subscription protocol state tracking\\n- `SotwSubscriptionState`: Tracks SotW subscription state, version info, and nonces\\n- `DeltaSubscriptionState`: Implements the delta xDS state machine with:\\n  - Resource version tracking (requested, wildcard, and ambiguous resource states)\\n  - Subscription interest updates\\n  - Resource addition/removal tracking\\n  - Initial request handling\\n  - Heartbeat support detection\\n\\nThe delta state machine handles resource versioning with three states:\\n- Requested resources: explicitly requested with their versions\\n- Wildcard resources: received via wildcard subscription\\n- Ambiguous resources: lost interest but possibly in wildcard\\n\\n## 4. Resource Subscription Watch Map\\n**Files**: `source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/watch_map.h/cc`\\n\\nThe `WatchMap` class manages multiple watches on xDS resources:\\n- Tracks which resource names are watched by which callers\\n- Implements the `UntypedConfigUpdateCallbacks` interface to receive updates from the mux\\n- Delivers updates to all interested watches\\n- Tracks additions/removals of resources for subscription interest updates\\n- Optionally caches resources (used for EDS)\\n\\n## 5. ACK/NACK Processing\\n**Files**: `source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/update_ack.h`, `pausable_ack_queue.h/cc`\\n\\n- `UpdateAck`: Holds nonce, type_url, and error_detail (for NACKs)\\n- `PausableAckQueue`: Special queue implementing head-of-line blocking mitigation:\\n  - Supports pausing/resuming individual resource type URLs\\n  - Ensures ordered delivery of ACKs/NACKs respecting paused types\\n  - Critical for ADS multiplexing where one resource type can be paused without blocking others\\n\\nThe ACK/NACK flow:\\n1. Server response received by mux\\n2. `handleResponse()` in SubscriptionState generates UpdateAck\\n3. Good responses generate ACKs (error_detail empty)\\n4. Bad responses generate NACKs (error_detail contains error code)\\n5. `getNextRequestWithAck()` adds ACK to next request\\n6. PausableAckQueue manages ordering with pause support\\n\\n## 6. Failover Support\\n**File**: `source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/grpc_mux_failover.h`\\n\\nThe `GrpcMuxFailover<RQ, RS>` template multiplexes between primary and failover gRPC streams, managing callbacks and stream switching.\\n\\n## 7. Factory and Subscription Components\\n**Files**: \\n- `grpc_mux_context.h`: Context structure passed to mux creation\\n- `grpc_subscription_factory.h/cc`: Creates appropriate subscription types (SotW/Delta/ADS)\\n- `grpc_subscription_impl.h/cc`: Individual subscription implementation\\n- `grpc_collection_subscription_factory.h/cc`: Collection subscription factory\\n\\n## 8. Resource Caching\\n**Files**: `source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/eds_resources_cache_impl.h/cc`\\n\\nEDS-specific resource cache for maintaining endpoint discovery state across updates.\\n\\n## 9. Null Implementation\\n**File**: `source/common/config/null_grpc_mux_impl.h`\\n\\nPlaceholder mux returned when ADS is not configured, throws exception on use.\\n\\n## Protocol Flow Summary\\n\\n1. **Stream Establishment**: `GrpcStream::establishNewStream()` creates bidirectional gRPC stream\\n2. **Resource Interest**: `WatchMap::updateWatchInterest()` tracks resource changes\\n3. **Request Generation**: `SubscriptionState::getNextRequestInternal()` creates discovery requests\\n4. **Response Processing**: `onDiscoveryResponse()` \u2192 `handleResponse()` \u2192 `WatchMap::onConfigUpdate()`\\n5. **ACK/NACK Generation**: `SubscriptionState::handleResponse()` returns `UpdateAck`\\n6. **Ordered Delivery**: `PausableAckQueue` ensures ACKs respect pause state\\n7. **Next Request**: `getNextRequestWithAck()` combines new request with ACK/NACK\\n\\nThe implementation supports both legacy and unified architectures, enabling gradual migration from separate SotW/Delta muxes to a unified template-based approach.\"\n}\n",

`grpc_stream_interface.h`\\n\\nThe `GrpcStream<RequestProto, ResponseProto>` template class manages the gRPC bidirectional streaming communication with the xDS management server. It handles stream establishment, message sending, rate limiting, reconnection with backoff, and status tracking. The `GrpcStreamInterface` provides the abstract interface for stream operations.\\n\\n## 2. Main gRPC Mux Implementations\\n\\n### Legacy Implementation (Two variants):\\n**Files**: `source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/grpc_mux_impl.h/cc`, `new_grpc_mux_impl.h/cc`\\n\\n- `GrpcMuxImpl` handles State-of-the-World (SotW) xDS protocol where the entire resource state is sent with each update\\n- `NewGrpcMuxImpl` handles Delta xDS protocol where only resource changes are sent\\n\\nThese manage subscription multiplexing, request queuing, and ACK/NACK handling.\\n\\n### Unified Implementation (New Architecture):\\n**Files**: `source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/xds_mux/grpc_mux_impl.h/cc`\\n\\nThe template-based `GrpcMuxImpl<S, F, RQ, RS>` provides a unified mux that handles both SotW and Delta variants through template parameters:\\n- `GrpcMuxSotw`: Specialization for SotW protocol\\n- `GrpcMuxDelta`: Specialization for Delta protocol\\n\\n## 3. Subscription State Machine (Resource Subscription Tracking)\\n**Files**: `source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/xds_mux/subscription_state.h`, `sotw_subscription_state.h/cc`, `delta_subscription_state.h/cc`\\n\\n- `BaseSubscriptionState<RS, RQ>`: Abstract base for subscription protocol state tracking\\n- `SotwSubscriptionState`: Tracks SotW subscription state, version info, and nonces\\n- `DeltaSubscriptionState`: Implements the delta xDS state machine with:\\n  - Resource version tracking (requested, wildcard, and ambiguous resource states)\\n  - Subscription interest updates\\n  - Resource addition/removal tracking\\n  - Initial request handling\\n  - Heartbeat support detection\\n\\nThe delta state machine handles resource versioning with three states:\\n- Requested resources: explicitly requested with their versions\\n- Wildcard resources: received via wildcard subscription\\n- Ambiguous resources: lost interest but possibly in wildcard\\n\\n## 4. Resource Subscription Watch Map\\n**Files**: `source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/watch_map.h/cc`\\n\\nThe `WatchMap` class manages multiple watches on xDS resources:\\n- Tracks which resource names are watched by which callers\\n- Implements the `UntypedConfigUpdateCallbacks` interface to receive updates from the mux\\n- Delivers updates to all interested watches\\n- Tracks additions/removals of resources for subscription interest updates\\n- Optionally caches resources (used for EDS)\\n\\n## 5. ACK/NACK Processing\\n**Files**: `source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/update_ack.h`, `pausable_ack_queue.h/cc`\\n\\n- `UpdateAck`: Holds nonce, type_url, and error_detail (for NACKs)\\n- `PausableAckQueue`: Special queue implementing head-of-line blocking mitigation:\\n  - Supports pausing/resuming individual resource type URLs\\n  - Ensures ordered delivery of ACKs/NACKs respecting paused types\\n  - Critical for ADS multiplexing where one resource type can be paused without blocking others\\n\\nThe ACK/NACK flow:\\n1. Server response received by mux\\n2. `handleResponse()` in SubscriptionState generates UpdateAck\\n3. Good responses generate ACKs (error_detail empty)\\n4. Bad responses generate NACKs (error_detail contains error code)\\n5. `getNextRequestWithAck()` adds ACK to next request\\n6. PausableAckQueue manages ordering with pause support\\n\\n## 6. Failover Support\\n**File**: `source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/grpc_mux_failover.h`\\n\\nThe `GrpcMuxFailover<RQ, RS>` template multiplexes between primary and failover gRPC streams, managing callbacks and stream switching.\\n\\n## 7. Factory and Subscription Components\\n**Files**: \\n- `grpc_mux_context.h`: Context structure passed to mux creation\\n- `grpc_subscription_factory.h/cc`: Creates appropriate subscription types (SotW/Delta/ADS)\\n- `grpc_subscription_impl.h/cc`: Individual subscription implementation\\n- `grpc_collection_subscription_factory.h/cc`: Collection subscription factory\\n\\n## 8. Resource Caching\\n**Files**: `source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/eds_resources_cache_impl.h/cc`\\n\\nEDS-specific resource cache for maintaining endpoint discovery state across updates.\\n\\n## 9. Null Implementation\\n**File**: `source/common/config/null_grpc_mux_impl.h`\\n\\nPlaceholder mux returned when ADS is not configured, throws exception on use.\\n\\n## Protocol Flow Summary\\n\\n1. **Stream Establishment**: `GrpcStream::establishNewStream()` creates bidirectional gRPC stream\\n2. **Resource Interest**: `WatchMap::updateWatchInterest()` tracks resource changes\\n3. **Request Generation**: `SubscriptionState::getNextRequestInternal()` creates discovery requests\\n4. **Response Processing**: `onDiscoveryResponse()` \u2192 `handleResponse()` \u2192 `WatchMap::onConfigUpdate()`\\n5. **ACK/NACK Generation**: `SubscriptionState::handleResponse()` returns `UpdateAck`\\n6. **Ordered Delivery**: `PausableAckQueue` ensures ACKs respect pause state\\n7. **Next Request**: `getNextRequestWithAck()` combines new request with ACK/NACK\\n\\nThe implementation supports both legacy and unified architectures, enabling gradual migration from separate SotW/Delta muxes to a unified template-based approach.\"\n}\n",
